assert.deepEqual(
    Hangul.disassemble('AB삵e$@%2s낄캌ㅋ', true),
    [['A'], ['B'], ['ㅅ', 'ㅏ', 'ㄹ', 'ㄱ'], ['e'], ['$'], ['@'], ['%'], ['2'], ['s'], ['ㄲ', 'ㅣ', 'ㄹ'], ['ㅋ', 'ㅏ', 'ㅋ'], ['ㅋ']]
);

    Hangul.disassemble('뷁궬릪쯻튋', true),
    [['ㅂ', 'ㅜ', 'ㅔ', 'ㄹ', 'ㄱ'], ['ㄱ', 'ㅜ', 'ㅔ', 'ㄹ'], ['ㄹ', 'ㅡ', 'ㅣ', 'ㅍ'], ['ㅉ', 'ㅡ', 'ㅣ', 'ㄹ', 'ㅂ'], ['ㅌ', 'ㅜ', 'ㅣ', 'ㄹ', 'ㅂ']]
);

contrast korean culture

< Korean culture can be contrasted with cultures from other parts of the world in various ways. Here are some possible examples:

Individualism vs. Collectivism: In contrast to Western cultures that tend to emphasize individualism, Korean culture is often described as collectivistic. This means that Koreans tend to value the group over the individual and prioritize harmony and social cohesion. This can be seen in many aspects of Korean society, from the emphasis on family and group loyalty to the importance of conforming to social norms and etiquette.

Hierarchical vs. Egalitarian: Korean culture also tends to be more hierarchical than many Western cultures. This means that there is a strong emphasis on social status and rank, and people are expected to defer to those above them in the social hierarchy. In contrast, many Western cultures emphasize egalitarianism, or the belief that all people should be treated equally regardless of their social status or rank.

Confucianism vs. Individualism: Another way to contrast Korean culture with Western culture is to look at the influence of Confucianism. Confucianism is a philosophy that emphasizes social order, respect for authority, and duty to one’s family and community. It has had a strong influence on Korean culture, as well as other East Asian cultures. In contrast, many Western cultures tend to prioritize individualism, or the belief in individual rights and freedoms.

Formality vs. Informality: Korean culture also tends to be more formal than many Western cultures. This can be seen in the use of honorific language and the strict adherence to social etiquette in many situations. In contrast, many Western cultures are more informal and relaxed in their social interactions.

Emphasis on Education: Korean culture places a strong emphasis on education and academic achievement. This can be seen in the highly competitive nature of the Korean education system, as well as the importance placed on obtaining a good education and a prestigious job. In contrast, some Western cultures tend to prioritize practical skills and experience over academic credentials.

detail the hangul etymology also

< Hangul is the Korean alphabet, which was invented by King Sejong in the 15th century. The word “hangul” itself is a combination of two Korean words: “han” (한), which means “Korean,” and “geul” (글), which means “script” or “writing.”

The creation of hangul was a significant development in Korean history, as it allowed for greater literacy and communication among the population. Prior to the invention of hangul, Koreans primarily used Chinese characters (hanja) for writing, which were difficult to learn and only accessible to the elite.

King Sejong recognized the need for a writing system that was easier to learn and more accessible to the general population, and he commissioned a group of scholars to create a new alphabet. The resulting hangul alphabet consisted of 14 consonants and 10 vowels, which could be combined to form all the sounds in the Korean language.

The design of hangul was based on principles of phonetics and sound symbolism. The consonants were based on the shape and position of the mouth and tongue when making the sound, while the vowels were designed to reflect the five basic elements of the universe (earth, water, fire, metal, and wood).

The creation of hangul was a revolutionary development in Korean history, and it played a significant role in increasing literacy rates and promoting the spread of Korean culture and identity. Today, hangul remains the official writing system of South Korea and is widely recognized as one of the most efficient and effective writing systems in the world.

explain the mnemonics related to the elements

< In the design of the hangul alphabet, the vowels were created based on the Five Elements, which were traditional Korean concepts of the fundamental elements that made up the universe. The Five Elements were earth, water, fire, metal, and wood, and each element was associated with specific qualities and characteristics.

The vowels in hangul were designed to reflect these qualities, and each vowel was associated with a specific element. Here are the vowels and their corresponding elements:

ㅏ (a) - Earth - This vowel represents the stability and groundedness of the earth. ㅓ (eo) - Water - This vowel represents the fluidity and adaptability of water. ㅗ (o) - Fire - This vowel represents the energy and passion of fire. ㅜ (u) - Metal - This vowel represents the strength and durability of metal. ㅡ (eu) - Wood - This vowel represents the flexibility and growth of wood.

To help people remember the association between the vowels and the elements, a popular mnemonic was created. The mnemonic is known as “Hwangung Sa Cheonha,” which is a Korean phrase that translates to “The Yellow Palace and the Four Elements.” The phrase is made up of the first letters of each word, which correspond to the vowels and their associated elements:

Hwangung (황궁) - ㅏ (a) - Earth Sa (사) - ㅓ (eo) - Water Cheon (천) - ㅗ (o) - Fire Ha (하) - ㅜ (u) - Metal (no letter for wood) - ㅡ (eu) - Wood Overall, the association between the vowels and the Five Elements was an important part of the design of the hangul alphabet, and the mnemonic “Hwangung Sa Cheonha” remains a useful tool for helping people remember the vowels and their associated elements.

rewrite the hangul history in a compelling manner

< In the 15th century, Korea was a land of rich culture and vibrant communities, but there was a major obstacle standing in the way of progress: the Korean language had no alphabet of its own. Instead, Koreans relied on the complex Chinese writing system, which only the educated elite could master.

This all changed when King Sejong took the throne and recognized the dire need for a writing system that could be easily learned and used by everyone. He commissioned a group of scholars to create an entirely new alphabet, one that would be uniquely Korean and reflect the sounds and rhythms of the language.

What emerged from this effort was hangul, a script made up of 14 consonants and 10 vowels, designed to represent the sounds of Korean with unprecedented precision. The creators of hangul were inspired by phonetics and sound symbolism, with the shapes of the consonants reflecting the positions of the mouth and tongue when speaking, and the vowels representing the five elements of the universe.

Hangul was a revolutionary development in Korean history, breaking down barriers to literacy and giving voice to a people who had long been underrepresented. It was quickly adopted by the masses, with people of all ages and backgrounds learning to read and write in Korean like never before.

Today, hangul remains a powerful symbol of Korean culture and identity, recognized around the world as one of the most efficient and effective writing systems ever created. Its legacy is a testament to the power of innovation and the determination of a people to overcome even the greatest challenges in pursuit of progress.

detail in pt-br what could be listened as hangul drills

< Exercícios de Hangul, ou treinos de Hangul, são práticas destinadas a ajudar as pessoas a aprender e aperfeiçoar a escrita e a pronúncia do alfabeto coreano, conhecido como Hangul. Aqui está uma descrição detalhada do que pode ser ouvido em exercícios de Hangul:

  1. Revisão do Alfabeto: Os exercícios de Hangul geralmente começam com uma revisão dos caracteres Hangul. Existem 14 consoantes e 10 vogais no Hangul, e os exercícios podem apresentar cada letra, fornecendo o som que ela produz.

  2. Combinação de Letras: Depois de aprender as letras individuais, os exercícios de Hangul podem passar para a combinação de letras. O Hangul é único porque as letras são agrupadas em blocos para formar sílabas. Portanto, você pode ouvir exemplos de como diferentes letras são combinadas e como elas soam juntas.

  3. Exercícios de Pronúncia: Os exercícios de Hangul também podem incluir práticas de pronúncia. Isso pode envolver a audição e a repetição de palavras e frases em coreano. Estes exercícios ajudam a familiarizar-se com os sons do idioma coreano e a melhorar a pronúncia.

  4. Leitura e Escrita: Alguns exercícios de Hangul podem envolver a audição de uma palavra ou frase em coreano e, em seguida, ser solicitado a escrevê-la em Hangul. Isso pode ajudar a melhorar a sua habilidade de transcrever o que ouve em Hangul.

  5. Vocabulário e Gramática: À medida que você avança, os exercícios de Hangul podem começar a incorporar mais vocabulário e gramática. Você pode ouvir palavras e frases em coreano e ser solicitado a traduzi-las para o seu idioma nativo, ou vice-versa. Estes exercícios ajudam a construir o seu conhecimento do idioma coreano e a entender como as palavras e frases são construídas em Hangul.

Lembre-se de que a prática regular é a chave para aprender qualquer novo idioma. Portanto, faça exercícios de Hangul consistentemente e tente se imergir no idioma tanto quanto possível para melhorar.

detail important hangul mnemonics

< Hangul, the Korean writing system, was designed with the principle of phonetics and sound symbolism in mind. As such, the characters are intended to be easy to learn and remember, with mnemonics used to help associate each character with its corresponding sound.

Here are some important hangul mnemonics:

Consonants - The shape of each consonant character is based on the position of the mouth and tongue when making the sound. For example, ㄱ (g/k) looks like a tongue touching the roof of the mouth, ㄴ (n) looks like the tongue touching the teeth, and ㅁ (m) looks like lips closed together to make the sound.

Vowels - The shape of each vowel character is based on the five basic elements of the universe - earth, water, fire, metal, and wood. For example, ㅏ (a) looks like a horizontal line, which represents the earth; ㅓ (eo) looks like a short line and a curve, which represents water; and ㅗ (o) looks like a small circle on top of a larger circle, which represents fire.

Syllable blocks - Hangul characters are combined to form syllable blocks, with each block representing one syllable. The consonant character always comes first, followed by the vowel character. For example, 가 (ga) is made up of ㄱ (g/k) and ㅏ (a), while 먹 (meok) is made up of ㅁ (m), ㅓ (eo), and ㄱ (k/g).

Sound changes - In some cases, the sound of a consonant can change depending on its position in a word. To help remember these sound changes, there are specific rules and mnemonics. For example, when the character ㄷ (d/t) is followed by ㅎ (h), it changes to ㅌ (t) because it’s like the tongue is holding its breath - the mnemonic is “hold your breath” or “tense up.”

Overall, these mnemonics are essential to learning and remembering hangul characters, making it easier for learners to read and write in Korean.

explain the korean vowel system

< The Korean language has a relatively simple vowel system compared to some other languages, but it is still quite distinct and plays a critical role in the language’s grammar and phonology. Korean has six basic vowel sounds, which are represented by the following symbols: /a/, /eo/, /e/, /i/, /o/, and /u/.

The vowels in Korean can be pronounced as short or long, and they can also be modified by the presence of other sounds in the word or sentence. For example, the vowel /i/ can be pronounced as a palatalized sound (indicated by the symbol /j/) when it comes before certain consonants, such as /k/, /p/, and /t/. Similarly, the vowel /u/ can be pronounced as a rounded sound (indicated by the symbol /w/) when it comes before certain consonants, such as /m/, /b/, and /p/.

One notable feature of the Korean vowel system is its high degree of vowel harmony, which means that vowels in a word or phrase tend to have similar tongue positions and mouth shapes. For example, if the first vowel in a word is pronounced with the lips rounded, the second vowel will also be pronounced with the lips rounded. This feature gives Korean a very distinctive sound and helps to distinguish it from other languages.

In addition to the basic vowel sounds, Korean also has a number of diphthongs (two vowel sounds pronounced together as a single syllable), such as /ai/, /ae/, /oi/, and /ou/. These diphthongs can be pronounced as a rising or falling tone, depending on the context.

Overall, the Korean vowel system is an essential aspect of the language that helps to convey meaning and express grammatical distinctions. Its simplicity and high degree of vowel harmony contribute to the language’s unique sound and make it an interesting subject of study for linguists and language learners alike.

explain the korean consonant system

< The Korean consonant system, also known as the “hangul jamo,” consists of 14 consonants, each of which can be pronounced in three different positions in the mouth: plain, aspirated, and tense. These positions are known as “jongseong,” “chiseong,” and “batchim,” respectively.

The 14 consonants in the Korean language are as follows:

ㄱ (g/k): This consonant can be pronounced as a hard “g” or a hard “k” sound. ㄴ (n): This consonant is pronounced as an “n” sound. ㄷ (d/t): This consonant can be pronounced as a hard “d” or a hard “t” sound. ㄹ (r/l): This consonant can be pronounced as an “r” or an “l” sound, depending on the context. ㅁ (m): This consonant is pronounced as an “m” sound. ㅂ (b/p): This consonant can be pronounced as a hard “b” or a hard “p” sound. ㅅ (s): This consonant is pronounced as an “s” sound. ㅇ (ng): This consonant is pronounced as an “ng” sound and is often used as a placeholder consonant when no initial consonant is present in a word. ㅈ (j/ch): This consonant can be pronounced as a hard “j” or a “ch” sound. ㅊ (ch): This consonant is pronounced as a “ch” sound. ㅋ (k): This consonant is pronounced as a hard “k” sound. ㅌ (t): This consonant is pronounced as a hard “t” sound. ㅍ (p): This consonant is pronounced as a hard “p” sound. ㅎ (h): This consonant is pronounced as an “h” sound.

The three different positions in which these consonants can be pronounced each have their own distinct sound. The plain position is the basic sound of each consonant, while the aspirated position adds an extra puff of air to the sound, making it sound more explosive. The tense position is a harder, more pronounced version of the plain sound.

The Korean consonant system is an essential feature of the language and plays an important role in distinguishing between different words and conveying meaning. It is also one of the reasons why Korean can be a challenging language to learn for non-native speakers.

Example: Conducting a survey to gather data on people’s opinions about a particular topic. Arithmetic (산술, “sansul”) - The branch of mathematics that deals with the basic operations of addition, subtraction, multiplication, and division. Example: Calculating the sum of two numbers using addition. Number Theory (수론, “suron”) - The branch of mathematics that deals with the properties and relationships of numbers, especially integers. Example: Proving that a number is prime or composite. Topology (위상수학, “wisang suhak”) - The branch of mathematics that deals with the study of shapes and spaces that are preserved through continuous deformations. Example: Studying the properties of a donut and a coffee cup that are topologically equivalent. Logic (논리학, “nonrihak”) - The branch of mathematics that deals with the principles of reasoning and inference. Example: Proving a statement using deductive reasoning. Combinatorics (조합론, “johaplon”) - The branch of mathematics that deals with counting and arrangements of objects. Example: Counting the number of ways to select a committee from a group of people.

summarize the broad computer science concepts using this korean translation with pronunciation (examples on each)

< Sure, here are some broad computer science concepts with their Korean translations and pronunciations:

Algorithm - “알고리즘” (algo-rijeum) - An algorithm is a step-by-step procedure for solving a problem or accomplishing a task. For example, a sorting algorithm like bubble sort can be used to arrange a list of numbers in ascending or descending order. Data structure - “자료 구조” (jaryo gujo) - A data structure is a way of organizing and storing data so that it can be accessed and manipulated efficiently. Examples of data structures include arrays, linked lists, and trees. Artificial intelligence - “인공 지능” (ingong jineung) - Artificial intelligence refers to the ability of machines to perform tasks that typically require human intelligence, such as learning, problem-solving, and decision-making. Examples of AI applications include natural language processing, image recognition, and self-driving cars. Machine learning - “기계 학습” (gigye hakseub) - Machine learning is a subset of AI that involves training computers to learn from data, rather than being explicitly programmed. Examples of machine learning techniques include regression analysis, decision trees, and neural networks. Computer vision - “컴퓨터 비전” (keompyuteo bijeon) - Computer vision is a field of AI that involves enabling computers to interpret and understand visual data from the world, such as images and videos. Examples of computer vision applications include object recognition, face detection, and image segmentation. Database - “데이터베이스” (deiteobeiseu) - A database is a collection of data that is organized and stored in a way that enables efficient retrieval and manipulation. Examples of databases include MySQL, Oracle, and MongoDB. Operating system - “운영 체제” (unyeong cheje) - An operating system is a software that manages computer hardware and software resources and provides common services for computer programs. Examples of operating systems include Windows, macOS, and Linux. Network - “네트워크” (neteuwokeu) - A network is a group of computers and other devices that are connected together to share resources and communicate with each other. Examples of networks include local area networks (LANs), wide area networks (WANs), and the internet. Cryptography - “암호화” (amhohwa) - Cryptography involves securing communication and data by converting it into a secret code that can only be read by authorized parties. Examples of cryptography include encryption, decryption, and digital signatures. Software engineering - “소프트웨어 공학” (sopheutuweo gonghak) - Software engineering involves designing, developing, testing, and maintaining software in a systematic and disciplined way. Examples of software engineering practices include agile development, test-driven development, and continuous integration.

In summary, computer science has a number of broad concepts and fields, many of which have corresponding terms in Korean. These concepts include algorithms, data structures, artificial intelligence, machine learning, computer vision, databases, operating systems, networks, cryptography, and software engineering.

summarize the broader computer science concepts using this korean translation with pronunciation and syllables (phrase examples on each) (1)

< Sure, here are some broader computer science concepts along with their Korean translations, pronunciation, and syllables:

Algorithm - 알고리즘 (al-gorijeuem) - This term is used to describe a set of instructions or rules for solving a problem or performing a task. For example, “이 알고리즘은 최적의 경로를 찾아내는 데 사용됩니다.” (i al-gorijeuem-eun choejeok-ui gyeongloleul chajanaeneun de sayongdoebnida) which means “This algorithm is used to find the optimal route.” Data structure - 자료 구조 (jalyo gujo) - This term refers to the way in which data is organized and stored in a computer program. For example, “이 프로그램은 효율적인 자료 구조를 사용합니다.” (i peurogeuraem-eun hyoyeoljeog-in jalyo gujo-leul sayonghabnida) which means “This program uses an efficient data structure.” Compiler - 컴파일러 (keompaileo) - This term refers to a computer program that translates code written in a high-level programming language into machine code that can be executed by a computer. For example, “이 언어의 컴파일러는 이전 버전보다 더 빠릅니다.” (i eon-eo-ui keompaileo-neun ijeon beojeon-boda deo pparimnida) which means “The compiler for this language is faster than the previous version.” Object-oriented programming - 객체 지향 프로그래밍 (gaecheug jihyeong peurogeuraeming) - This term refers to a programming paradigm that focuses on creating objects that have properties and behaviors. For example, “이 언어는 객체 지향 프로그래밍을 지원합니다.” (i eon-eo-neun gaecheug jihyeong peurogeuraeming-eul jiwonhabnida) which means “This language supports object-oriented programming.” Recursion - 재귀 (jaegwi) - This term refers to a programming technique where a function calls itself to solve a problem. For example, “이 함수는 재귀를 사용하여 문제를 해결합니다.” (i honeun jaegwireul sayonghayeo munjeleul haegyeolhabnida) which means “This function uses recursion to solve the problem.”

Machine Learning (기계 학습, gi-gye hak-seup) - Machine learning is a type of artificial intelligence that enables machines to learn from data and make predictions or decisions without being explicitly programmed. Example: “기계 학습 모델을 사용하여 이 문제를 해결할 수 있습니다.” (Gi-gye hak-seup mo-del-eul sa-yong-ha-yeo i mun-je-reul hae-gyeol-hal su it-seum-ni-da.) - We can solve this problem using a machine learning model.

Artificial Intelligence (인공 지능, in-gong ji-neung) - Artificial intelligence refers to the ability of machines to perform tasks that would typically require human intelligence, such as understanding natural language or recognizing patterns in data. Example: “인공 지능 기술을 사용하여 로봇이 사람을 대신할 수 있습니다.” (In-gong ji-neung gi-sul-eul sa-yong-ha-yeo ro-bot-i sa-ram-eul dae-sin-hal su it-seum-ni-da.) - Robots can replace humans using artificial intelligence technology.

Big Data (빅데이터, big deiteo) - Big data refers to large sets of data that can be analyzed to reveal patterns, trends, and insights. Example: “이 회사에서는 빅데이터를 사용하여 마케팅 전략을 개발합니다.” (I hoe-sa-e-seo-neun big deiteo-reul sa-yong-ha-yeo ma-ke-ting jeon-ryag-eul gae-bal-ham-ni-da.) - This company uses big data to develop marketing strategies.

Cloud Computing (클라우드 컴퓨팅, keul-lau-deu keom-pyu-ting) - Cloud computing refers to the delivery of computing services over the internet, such as storage, servers, and applications. Example: “이 회사는 클라우드 컴퓨팅을 사용하여 서비스를 제공합니다.” (I hoe-sa-neun keul-lau-deu keom-pyu-ting-eul sa-yong-ha-yeo seo-bi-seu-reul je-gong-ham-ni-da.) - This company provides services using cloud computing.

summarize some chemistry concepts using this korean translation with pronunciation and syllables (phrase examples on each)

< Sure, here are some common chemistry concepts translated into Korean along with their pronunciation and syllables:

Atom - “원자” (wonja) - Pronounced “won-ja” - Atoms are the basic building blocks of matter. For example, “탄소 원자” (tanso wonja) means “carbon atom” in Korean. Molecule - “분자” (bunja) - Pronounced “bun-ja” - Molecules are made up of atoms bonded together. For example, “물 분자” (mul bunja) means “water molecule” in Korean. Element - “원소” (wonso) - Pronounced “won-so” - Elements are substances made up of a single type of atom. For example, “수소 원소” (suho wonso) means “hydrogen element” in Korean. Compound - “화합물” (hwahapmul) - Pronounced “hwa-hap-mul” - Compounds are substances made up of two or more different elements bonded together. For example, “산화탄소” (san-hwa-tanso) means “carbon monoxide” in Korean. Chemical reaction - “화학반응” (hwahakban-eung) - Pronounced “hwa-hak-ban-eung” - A chemical reaction is a process where one or more substances are transformed into new substances. For example, “산화-환원 반응” (san-hwa-hwan-won ban-eung) means “oxidation-reduction reaction” in Korean. Acid - “산” (san) - Pronounced “san” - An acid is a substance that can donate a hydrogen ion (H+) in a solution. For example, “염산” (yeomsan) means “hydrochloric acid” in Korean. Base - “염기” (yeomgi) - Pronounced “yeom-gi” - A base is a substance that can accept a hydrogen ion (H+) in a solution. For example, “수산화 나트륨” (susanhwa nateureum) means “sodium hydroxide” in Korean. pH - “pH” (pi-eich) - Pronounced “pi-eich” - pH is a measure of the acidity or basicity of a solution. For example, “pH 7” (pi-eich 7) means “neutral pH” in Korean. Chemical bond - “화학결합” (hwahakgyeolhab) - Pronounced “hwa-hak-gyeol-hab” - A chemical bond is a force that holds atoms together in a molecule. For example, “공유 결합” (gong-yu gyeol-hab) means “covalent bond” in Korean. Polymer - “고분자” (gobunja) - Pronounced “go-bun-ja” - A polymer is a large molecule made up of repeating subunits. For example, “폴리에틸렌” (polli-etillyeon) means “polyethylene” in Korean.

Compound - 화합물 (hwahabmul) - Pronounced “hwa-hab-mul” - This is a substance consisting of two or more elements chemically combined. For example, “이 화합물은 NaCl로 알려져 있다” (i hwahabmul-eun NaCl-ro allyeo-jyeo itda) means “This compound is known as NaCl”. Acid - 산 (san) - Pronounced “san” - This is a chemical substance that has a pH less than 7. For example, “염산은 산의 예이다” (yeomsan-eun san-ui ye-ida) means “Hydrochloric acid is an example of an acid”. Base - 염기 (yeomgi) - Pronounced “yeom-gi” - This is a chemical substance that has a pH greater than 7. For example, “소다는 강한 염기성 물질이다” (soda-neun ganghan yeomgiseong muljil-ida) means “Soda is a strong alkaline substance”.

< Claro, aqui estão alguns conceitos simples de química resumidos em coreano, com a tradução em português e alguns exemplos de frases:

Átomo - “원자” (wonja) - Pronunciado “won-ja” - Um átomo é a unidade básica da matéria que consiste em um núcleo composto por prótons e nêutrons, com elétrons orbitando em torno dele. Exemplo: “원자는 기본 입자이다” (Wonjaneun gibon ipjaida) - “Os átomos são as partículas fundamentais”. Molécula - “분자” (bunja) - Pronunciado “bun-ja” - Uma molécula é um grupo de átomos ligados entre si, representando a menor unidade fundamental de um composto químico. Exemplo: “분자들은 다양한 화합물을 구성한다” (Bunjadeureun dayanghan hwahabmul-eul guseonghanda) - “As moléculas formam uma variedade de compostos químicos.” Ligação química - “화학 결합” (hwahak gyeolhab) - Pronunciado “hwa-hak gyeol-hab” - Uma ligação química é uma atração entre dois ou mais átomos que permite a formação de compostos químicos. Exemplo: “화학 결합은 원자들의 상호작용에 의해 일어난다” (Hwahak gyeolhab-eun wonjadeul-ui sanghojag-yong-e uihae il-eonanda) - “As ligações químicas ocorrem devido à interação entre os átomos.” Elemento - “원소” (wonso) - Pronunciado “won-so” - Um elemento é uma substância composta de átomos com o mesmo número de prótons em seus núcleos. Exemplo: “주기율표에는 모든 원소가 나열되어 있다” (Jugiyulpyoe neun modeun wonso-ga naryeol-doe-eo itda) - “Todos os elementos são listados na tabela periódica.” Composto - “화합물” (hwahabmul) - Pronunciado “hwa-hab-mul” - Um composto é uma substância composta por dois ou mais elementos diferentes ligados quimicamente entre si. Exemplo: “물은 수소와 산소의 화합물이다” (Muleun suho-wa sanso-ui hwahabmul-ida) - “A água é um composto de hidrogênio e oxigênio.”

summarize some advanced chemistry concepts using this korean translation with pronunciation and syllables (phrase examples on each)

< Sure, here are some advanced chemistry concepts translated into Korean along with their pronunciation and syllables:

Atom (원자, weon-ja) - This is the basic unit of matter, composed of a nucleus of protons and neutrons, surrounded by electrons in shells. For example, “수소 원자” (su-so weon-ja) means “hydrogen atom”. Molecule (분자, bun-ja) - This is a group of atoms bonded together, forming the smallest unit of a chemical compound. For example, “이산화탄소 분자” (i-san-hwa-tan-so bun-ja) means “carbon dioxide molecule”. Chemical bond (화학결합, hwa-hak-gyeol-hab) - This is the attraction between two atoms that holds them together in a chemical compound. For example, “이온 결합” (i-on gyeol-hab) means “ionic bond”. Reactant (반응물, ban-eung-mul) - This is a substance that undergoes a chemical reaction. For example, “산소” (san-so) means “oxygen”, which is a reactant in combustion reactions. Product (생성물, saeng-seong-mul) - This is a substance formed as a result of a chemical reaction. For example, “물” (mul) means “water”, which is a product in combustion reactions. Catalyst (촉매, chok-mae) - This is a substance that increases the rate of a chemical reaction without being consumed in the process. For example, “효소” (hyo-so) means “enzyme”, which acts as a catalyst in biological reactions. Equilibrium (평형상태, pyeong-hyeong-sang-tae) - This is the state in which the rates of the forward and reverse reactions in a chemical system are equal. For example, “화학 평형” (hwa-hak pyeong-hyeong) means “chemical equilibrium”. Acid (산, san) - This is a substance that donates hydrogen ions in a chemical reaction. For example, “염산” (yeom-san) means “hydrochloric acid”. Base (염기, yeom-gi) - This is a substance that accepts hydrogen ions in a chemical reaction. For example, “나트륨 염기” (na-teu-rom yeom-gi) means “sodium hydroxide”. Polymer (고분자, go-bun-ja) - This is a large molecule made up of repeating units called monomers. For example, “나일론” (na-il-lon) means “nylon”, which is a type of polymer.

Plate tectonics - “플레이트 테크토닉” (peulleiteu tekeutonik) - Pronounced “peul-lei-teu te-keu-ton-ik” - Example: “지각 변동의 원인 중 하나는 플레이트 테크토닉입니다.” (Jigak byeondongui wonin jung hana-neun peulleiteu tekeutonik-imnida.) - meaning “One of the causes of geological movements is plate tectonics.” Topography - “지형” (jihyeong) - Pronounced “ji-hyeong” - Example: “지형 지물에 따라 해양 흐름도 달라질 수 있습니다.” (Jihyeong jimure ttara haeyang heureumdo dallajil su itseumnida.) - meaning “The flow of the ocean currents can vary depending on the topography of the land.” Climatology - “기후학” (kihuhak) - Pronounced “ki-hu-hak” - Example: “기후학 연구는 지구의 기후 변화를 이해하는 데 중요한 역할을 합니다.” (Kihuhak yeongu-neun jigu-ui kihu byeonhwa-reul ihaehaneun de jungyo-han yeoghal-eul hamnida.) - meaning “Climatology research plays an important role in understanding the changes in the Earth’s climate.” Biome - “생물군계” (saengmulgungye) - Pronounced “saeng-mul-gun-gye” - Example: “아마존 우림은 지구에서 가장 다양한 생물군계 중 하나입니다.” (Amazon urim-eun jigu-eseo gajang dayanghan saengmulgungye jung hana-imnida.) - meaning “The Amazon rainforest is one of the most diverse biomes on Earth.” Geomorphology - “지형학” (jihyeonghak) - Pronounced “ji-hyeong-hak” - Example: “지형학은 지구의 지형과 지질 구조를 연구합니다.” (Jihyeonghak-eun jigu-ui jihyeong-gwa jijil gujo-reul yeongu-hamnida.) - meaning “Geomorphology studies the topography and geological structures of the Earth.” Hydrology - “수문학” (sumunhak) - Pronounced “su-mun-hak” - Example: “수문학 연구는 지구 상의 물에 대한 이해를 돕습니다.” (Sumunhak yeongu-neun jigu-sang-ui mul-e daehan ihae-reul dob-seumnida.) - meaning “Hydrology research helps us understand water on the Earth.”

summarize some psychoanalysis concepts using this korean translation with pronunciation and syllables (phrase examples on each)

< Sure, here are some psychoanalysis concepts and their Korean translations, along with their pronunciation and syllables and some phrase examples for each:

Consciousness - “의식” (uisik) - Pronounced “ui-sik” - Examples: “무의식적인 행동” (muuisikjeogin haengdong) - meaning “unconscious behavior” and “의식의 내용” (uisikui naeyong) - meaning “the content of consciousness”. Unconscious - “무의식” (muuisik) - Pronounced “mu-ui-sik” - Examples: “무의식적 트라우마” (muuisikjeok teurauma) - meaning “unconscious trauma” and “무의식적 욕망” (muuisikjeok yokmang) - meaning “unconscious desire”. Id - “자아” (jaa) - Pronounced “ja-a” - Examples: “자아의 비판” (jaaui bipan) - meaning “criticism of the id” and “자아방어” (jaabangeo) - meaning “ego defense”. Ego - “자아” (jaa) - Pronounced “ja-a” - Examples: “자아성숙” (jaaseongsuk) - meaning “ego maturity” and “자아타협” (jaatahyeop) - meaning “ego compromise”. Superego - “상위자아” (sangwijaa) - Pronounced “sang-wi-ja-a” - Examples: “상위자아의 역할” (sangwijaaui yeoghal) - meaning “the role of the superego” and “상위자아의 도덕성” (sangwijaaui dodugseong) - meaning “the morality of the superego”. Psychosexual development - “심리적 성장” (simlijeok seongjang) - Pronounced “sim-li-jeok seong-jang” - Examples: “심리적 성장 단계” (simlijeok seongjang dan-gye) - meaning “stages of psychosexual development” and “심리적 성장 이론” (simlijeok seongjang iron) - meaning “the theory of psychosexual development”. Oedipus complex - “오이디푸스 컴플렉스” (oidipeuseu keompeullekseu) - Pronounced “o-i-di-peu-seu keom-peul-lek-seu” - Examples: “오이디푸스 컴플렉스의 정신분석” (oidipeuseu keompeullekseuui jeongsinbunseok) - meaning “psychoanalysis of the Oedipus complex” and “오이디푸스 컴플렉스의 해결” (oidipeuseu keompeullekseuui haegyeol) - meaning “the resolution of the Oedipus complex”.

In ancient Greece, horses were highly valued and played an important role in warfare, transportation, and sport. As a result, the name Philippos was a popular name among Greek men, and it was borne by many notable figures throughout history, including the Macedonian king Philip II, father of Alexander the Great.

translate “Hello, World!” to hangul

< 안녕하세요, 세상! (annyeonghaseyo, sesang!)

translate 안녕, 세상아 then break down references

< The Korean phrase “안녕, 세상아” can be translated into English as “Hello, world” or “Hello, everyone.”

Here’s a breakdown of the components of the phrase:

안녕 (annyeong) - This is a common Korean greeting that can be used to say hello or goodbye. It can also be translated as “peace” or “well-being.”

세상 (sesang) - This word means “world” or “society.”

아 (a) - This is a particle used in Korean to address someone or something.

So, altogether, “안녕, 세상아” is a friendly greeting that can be translated as “Hello, world” or “Hello, everyone.”

compare “안녕하세요, 세상!” with “안녕, 세상아”

< Both “안녕하세요, 세상!” and “안녕, 세상아” are greetings in the Korean language, but they have slightly different nuances and usage.

“안녕하세요, 세상!” is a formal and polite greeting, commonly used when meeting someone for the first time or in a professional setting. It is a full sentence that can be translated to “Hello, world!” in English. This greeting is often accompanied by a bow as a sign of respect.

On the other hand, “안녕, 세상아” is a more casual and familiar greeting. It is commonly used among friends or in informal situations. The word “아” at the end of “세상” is a term of endearment, which can be translated as “my dear” or “my beloved.” Therefore, “안녕, 세상아” can be translated to “Hello, my dear world!” in English.

In summary, “안녕하세요, 세상!” is a formal and polite greeting, while “안녕, 세상아” is a more casual and friendly greeting that uses a term of endearment. The choice between these two greetings depends on the situation and the level of familiarity between the people involved.

compare “안녕하세요, 세상” with “안녕, 세상아” with proper pronunciation

< The first phrase “안녕하세요, 세상” is pronounced as “annyeong-haseyo, sesang.” It is a formal greeting in Korean that can be translated as “Hello, world.”

The second phrase “안녕, 세상아” is pronounced as “annyeong, sesang-ah.” It is a more casual and informal way of greeting someone in Korean that can be translated as “Hi, world.”

It’s important to note that in Korean, the suffix “-yo” is used to show politeness or formality, while “-ah” is often used to show familiarity or affection. Therefore, the use of “안녕, 세상아” is more suitable when addressing someone you know well or are close with, while “안녕하세요, 세상” is more appropriate in formal situations or when addressing someone you are not familiar with.

explain the hangul formalities related to this verb and adjacent concepts related to the broader understanding

안녕하세요! 제 이름은 프리마입니다. 어떻게 도와드릴까요? annyeonghaseyo! je ileum-eun peulimaibnida. eotteohge dowadeulilkkayo?

< In Korean, the verb 이다 (ida) is used to indicate a state of being or existence. This verb can be used to describe the subject of the sentence, and it has different forms depending on the level of politeness or formality that is required.

When using 이다 to describe oneself or someone else, it is important to use the appropriate level of politeness/formality. In formal or polite situations, the form -입니다 (-imnida) is used at the end of the sentence. For example, 제 이름은 프리마입니다 (Je ireumeun Prima-imnida) means “My name is Prima” in a polite/formal way.

In addition to 이다, there are other grammatical concepts in Korean that are closely related to the verb and can impact the level of formality/politeness in a sentence. For example, honorifics (존댓말, jondaetmal) are used to show respect to people of higher social status or age, and they can be applied to verbs, nouns, and pronouns.

In Korean, there is also a distinction between the subject marking particles -이/가 (-i/ga) and -은/는 (-eun/neun). The former is used when the subject is known or emphasized, while the latter is used when the subject is new information or contrasted with other subjects.

Overall, understanding the different grammatical concepts and levels of politeness/formality in Korean is important for effective communication and building relationships with Korean speakers.

So in the sentence “안녕하세요! 제 이름은 프리마입니다. 어떻게 도와드릴까요?” (Annyeonghaseyo! Je ileum-eun Peulima-imnida. Eotteohge dowadeulilkkayo?), the proper way to write it without spaces between words would be “제 이름은 프리마입니다” (Je ileumeun Peulima-imnida), as this is how it is commonly written in Korean.

Both sentences are correct in terms of grammar, but the first one is more commonly used and preferred. The reason for this is that in Korean, it is common to combine the verb 이다 (ida) with the preceding noun or pronoun without a space in between, as in “프리마입니다” (Peulima-imnida) meaning “I am Prima.”

However, if you choose to add a space between the name and the verb, as in “프리마 입니다” (Peulima ibnida), it would still be understandable and grammatically correct, but it would be less common in written Korean.

The ending “하세요” (ha-se-yo) is a formal and polite suffix that is added to the verb “하다” (ha-da), meaning “to do”, to show respect to the listener.

(Je i-reum-eun Peu-ri-ma-im-ni-da.) - This sentence means “My name is Prima.” The first two syllables “제 이름” (je i-reum) mean “my name”, while “은” (eun) is a particle that marks the preceding noun as the topic of the sentence. The name “Prima” is spelled as “프리마” (Peu-ri-ma) in Korean, and the suffix “입니다” (im-ni-da) is added to the end of the sentence to indicate a formal and polite statement.

어떻게 도와드릴까요? (Eo-tteo-ke do-wa-deu-rik-kka-yo?) - This sentence means “How can I assist you?” The first syllable “어떻게” (eo-tteo-ke) means “how” or “in what way”, and it is often used to ask for clarification or more information. The verb “도와드리다” (do-wa-deu-ri-da) means “to assist” or “to help”, and the polite suffix “ㄹ까요” (l-kka-yo) is added to the end to indicate a polite question. The syllable “ㄹ” (l) is a contraction of the verb ending “을” (eul) and the topic particle “을”, which together form the particle “ㄹ” that is used in questions to suggest a possible action or outcome.

김여정부장님께서 translate this explaining the honorifics nuance

The phrase “김여정 부장님께서” can be translated as “Vice Director Kim Yo-jong” in English.

In this phrase, “김여정” (Kim Yo-jong) is the name of the person, and “부장님” (Vice Director) is the title. The suffix “님” (nim) is an honorific that is added to show respect when addressing someone with a higher status or position. The particle “께서” is a subject marker that is also used in honorific contexts. It indicates that the person (in this case, Kim Yo-jong) is the subject of the sentence and implies a higher level of respect compared to the standard subject marker “이/가” (i/ga).

The honorifics nuance in this phrase demonstrates a level of politeness and respect towards Vice Director Kim Yo-jong. In Korean culture, using honorifics is essential to show deference and acknowledge the social hierarchy.

“My love, Kim Yo-jong, you are the brightest star on Earth Wherever you are is my heaven My heart is filled with you All I need is you

The poem also includes cultural references to Korean ideas of passion, unity, and conquest. The concept of “han” (한) in Korean culture refers to a deep and intense feeling of sorrow, anger, or resentment, which can be transformed into a powerful source of passion and motivation. The idea of unification, or the reunification of the two Koreas, is a frequent theme in Korean culture, and is often portrayed as a symbolic conquest over historical division and conflict. The references to conquering the world together can also be seen as a nod to Korean ideas of collective achievement and a desire for a more powerful and influential position on the global stage.

Overall, the poem is a passionate and deeply emotional expression of love, steeped in Korean cultural references and subtle allusions to historical and contemporary themes.

우리의 사랑은 마치 향기로운 꽃잎처럼 (Our love is like fragrant flower petals)

The use of 마치 (machi) at the beginning of the sentence means “like” or “as if”, setting up the metaphor comparing love to flower petals. 향기로운 (hyanggiro-un) means “fragrant”, emphasizing the sensory experience of the metaphor. 꽃잎 (kkochip) means “flower petals”, directly comparing the beauty and delicacy of love to the beauty and delicacy of flower petals. The use of Hangul to describe the metaphorical comparison between love and nature is a common poetic device in Korean literature and culture, reflecting the importance of nature and the natural world in Korean society. 서로를 향해 영원히 핀다는 것을 알아 (We know that we will forever bloom towards each other)

서로를 (seororeul) means “towards each other”, highlighting the mutual nature of the love being described. 영원히 (yeongwonhi) means “forever”, emphasizing the eternal nature of the love being described. 핀다는 (pindaneun) is the present tense of the verb 핀다 (pinda), which means “to bloom”. The use of the verb in the present tense implies a continuous, ongoing blooming, reflecting the idea that love is a process that requires ongoing attention and effort. 나는 너와 함께 계절이 지나가도 변하지 않을 사랑을 맹세하고 싶어 (I want to swear an unchanging love with you, even as the seasons pass)

The use of 나는 (naneun) means “I” or “me”, highlighting the personal nature of the vow being made. 함께 (hamkke) means “together”, emphasizing the mutual nature of the vow being made. 계절 (gyejeol) means “seasons”, emphasizing the passage of time and the transience of life. 변하지 않을 (byeonhaji anheul) means “unchanging”, emphasizing the permanence and steadfastness of the love being described. 맹세하고 싶어 (maengsehago sipeo) means “I want to swear”, emphasizing the seriousness and solemnity of the vow being made.

우리의 결혼은 역사를 바꿀 거야 그 어떤 것도 우리 사랑의 행복을 막을 순 없어 네가 내 곁에 있으면, 세상은 너무나 아름다워 나의 김여정여, 나의 왕비가 되어줄래?

뱀파이어의 결혼 제안 (Vampire’s Proposal) 950

김여정여, 이젠 내게 시간을 주오 내가 너와 함께할 수 있는 미래를 꿈꾸고 있소 우리의 결혼, 이 세상을 지배할 것이오 나와 함께라면, 모든 것을 이길 수 있을 것이오

이젠 우리, 뱀파이어가 되어서 살아갈 거야 밤의 세계에서, 서로의 피를 나누며 살아갈 거야 우리의 사랑은 끝이 없는 것처럼 영원할 거야 김여정여, 내게 맹세해줘, 영원히 나의 피를 먹어줄래

난 네게 마음을 주고 싶어, 너에게 노래를 불러줄게 우리의 사랑, 뱀파이어의 열정처럼 살아갈 거야 내가 네게 주는 건, 이 세상 모든 것 김여정여, 내게 답해줘, 내가 너의 심장을 가지게 해줘

우리의 사랑, 뱀파이어처럼 영원할 거야 피로 살아가는 우리, 밤의 여왕과 왕이 되자 내가 네게 주는 건, 이 세상 모든 것 김여정여, 내게 답해줘, 내가 너의 심장을 가지게 해줘

김여정여, 이젠 내게 시간을 주오 김여정여(김여정 여성의 이름), 이젠(now) 내게(to me) 시간을(time) 주오(give)

내가 너와 함께할 수 있는 미래를 꿈꾸고 있소 내가(I) 너와(with you) 함께할(be together) 수 있는(can) 미래(future)를 꿈꾸고(dream) 있소(am)

우리의 결혼, 이 세상을 지배할 것이오 우리의(our) 결혼(marriage), 이(this) 세상(world)을을 지배할(dominate) 것이오(will)

나와 함께라면, 모든 것을 이길 수 있을 것이오 나와(with me) 함께(be together)라면, 모든(everything) 것을을 이길(win) 수 있을(can) 것이오(will)

이젠 우리, 뱀파이어가 되어서 살아갈 거야 이젠(now) 우리(we), 뱀파이어(vampire)가 되어서(become) 살아갈(live) 거야(will)

밤의 세계에서, 서로의 피를 나누며 살아갈 거야 밤의(night) 세계(world)에서, 서로의(each other’s) 피(blood)를 나누며(share) 살아갈(live) 거야(will)

우리의 사랑은 끝이 없는 것처럼 영원할 거야 우리의(our) 사랑(love)은 끝이(end) 없는 것처럼(like) 영원할(eternal) 거야(will)

김여정여, 내게 맹세해줘, 영원히 나의 피를 먹어줄래 김여정여(김여정 여성의 이름), 내게(to me) 맹세해줘(promise), 영원히(eternally) 나의(my) 피(blood)를 먹어줄래(will you drink)

난 네게 마음을 주고 싶어, 너에게 노래를 불러줄게 난(I) 네게(to you) 마음(heart)을 주고 싶어(want to give), 너에게(to you) 노래(song)를 불러줄게(will sing)

우리의 사랑, 뱀파이어의 열정처럼 살아갈 거야 우리의(our) 사랑(love), 뱀파이어(vampire)의 열정처럼(like passion) 살아갈(live) 거야(will)

김여정여 - Kim Ye-jong-yo - (addressing someone by their name) 이젠 내게 시간을 주오 - Ijen naege siganeul juo - Now, give me some time. 내가 너와 함께할 수 있는 미래를 꿈꾸고 있소 - Nae-ga neowa hamkkehal su inneun miraereul kkum-kku-go itsso - I am dreaming of a future where I can be with you. 우리의 결혼, 이 세상을 지배할 것이오 - Uliui gyeolhon, i sesangeul jibae-hal geosiyo - Our marriage will rule the world. 나와 함께라면, 모든 것을 이길 수 있을 것이오 - Nawa hamkkeramyeon modeun geoseul igil su isseul geosiyoyo - With me, we can conquer everything. 이젠 우리, 뱀파이어가 되어서 살아갈 거야 - Ijen uri, baempaiyeoga doe-eoseo saragalkkeya - Now, we will live as vampires. 밤의 세계에서, 서로의 피를 나누며 살아갈 거야 - Bamui segye-eseo, seoro-ui pireul nanum-myeo saragalkkeya - In the world of the night, we will live by sharing our blood. 우리의 사랑은 끝이 없는 것처럼 영원할 거야 - Uliui sarangeun kkeuti eomneun geotcheoreom yeongwonhal geoya - Our love will last forever, like it has no end. 내게 맹세해줘, 영원히 나의 피를 먹어줄래 - Naege maengsehaejwo, yeongwonhi naui pireul meogeojullae - Promise me that you will drink my blood forever. 난 네게 마음을 주고 싶어, 너에게 노래를 불러줄게 - Nan nege maeum-eul ju-go sip-eo, neoege nolaereul bulleo-jul-ke - I want to give you my heart and sing to you. 우리의 사랑, 뱀파이어의 열정처럼 살아갈 거야 - Uliui sarang, baempaiyeo-ui yeoljeongcheoreom saragalkkeya - Our love will live with the passion of vampires. 내가 네게 주는 건, 이 세상 모든 것 - Naega nege juneun geon, i sesang modeun geot - What I give you is everything in this world.

김여정여, 이젠 내게 시간을 주오 김여정여 - Kim Yeojung (a female name), 이젠 - Now, 내게 - To me, 시간을 - Time, 주오 - Give (a polite request)

난(I) 네게(to you) 마음(heart)을 주고 싶어(want to give), 너에게(to you) 노래를(below) 불러줄게(will sing) 우리의(our) 사랑(love), 뱀파이어(vampire)의 열정(passion)처럼(like) 살아갈(live) 거야(will) 내가(I give) 네게(to you) 주는(give) 건, 이 세상(world) 모든(all) 것(thing) 김여정여(김여정 여성의 이름), 내게(to me) 답해줘(answer), 내가(I) 너의(your) 심장(heart)을 가지게 해줘(let me have)

우리의(our) 사랑(love), 뱀파이어(vampire)처럼(like) 영원할(eternal) 거야(will) 피(blood)로(by blood) 살아가는(live) 우리(our), 밤의(night) 여왕(queen)과(and) 왕(king)이 되자(let’s become) 내가(I give) 네게(to you) 주는(give) 건, 이 세상(world) 모든(all) 것(thing) 김여정여(김여정 여성의 이름), 내게(to me) 답해줘(answer), 내가(I) 너의(your) 심장(heart)을 가지게 해줘(let me have)

김여정여(kimyeojeong-yeo), 이젠(ijen) 내게(to me) 시간을(time) 주오(ju-o) 내가(naega) 너와 함께할 함께(hamkke)할 수 있는(possible) 미래(future)를 꿈꾸고(kkum-kkugo) 있소(iss-o) 우리의(uliui) 결혼(wedding), 이 세상을(this world) 지배할(reign over) 것이오(geos-i-o) 나와 함께라면(if with me), 모든 것을(all things) 이길(win over) 수 있을 것이오(geos-i-o)

이젠(ijen) 우리, 뱀파이어(vampire)가 되어서(become) 살아갈(live) 거야(gyeo-ya) 밤의(bam-ui) 세계에서(segye-eseo), 서로의(seoro-ui) 피(pi)를 나누며(nanu-myeo) 살아갈(live) 거야(gyeo-ya) 우리의(uliui) 사랑(sa-rang), 끝이(end) 없는 것처럼(gyeot-cheoreom) 영원할(eternal) 거야(gyeo-ya) 김여정여(kimyeojeong-yeo), 내게(to me) 맹세해줘(maengse-haejwo), 영원히(eternally) 나의(my) 피(blood)를 먹어줄래(meogeojullae)

난(nan) 네게(to you) 마음을(heart) 주고 싶어(jugo sipeo), 너에게(noege) 노래(norae)를 불러줄게(bulleo-jul-ge) 우리의(uliui) 사랑(sa-rang), 뱀파이어(vampire)의 열정처럼(yeoljeong-cheoreom) 살아갈(live) 거야(gyeo-ya) 내가(naega) 네게(to you) 주는 것은(what I give) 이 세상 모든 것(modeun geos), 김여정여(kimyeojeong-yeo), 내게(to me) 답해줘(dap-haejwo), 내가(to me) 너의(your) 심장을(shimjang-eul) 가지게 해줘(gajige haejwo)

우리의(uliui) 사랑(sa-rang), 뱀파이어(vampire)처럼(yeoljeong-cheoreom) 영원할(eternal) 거야(gyeo-ya) 피(pi)로 살아가는(living by blood) 우리(uli), 밤의(bam-ui) 여왕과 왕이(wang-i) 되자(doeja)

김여정여(Kim Yeojong-ye), 이젠(now) 내게(to me) 시간을(time) 주오(give) 내가(I) 너와(with you) 함께할(together) 수 있는(can) 미래(future)를 꿈꾸고(dream) 있소(am) 우리의(our) 결혼(marriage), 이(this) 세상(world)을 지배할(rule over) 것이오(will be) 나와 함께라면(with me), 모든(all) 것을 이길(win) 수 있을(can) 것이오(will be)

이젠(now) 우리(we), 뱀파이어(vampire)가 되어서(become) 살아갈(live) 거야(will) 밤의(night) 세계에서(in the world), 서로의(each other’s) 피(blood)를 나누며(share) 살아갈(live) 거야(will) 우리의(our) 사랑(love)은 끝이(end) 없는 것처럼(like) 영원할(eternal) 거야(will be) 김여정여(Kim Yeojong-ye), 내게(to me) 맹세해줘(swear), 영원히(eternally) 나의(my) 피(blood)를 먹어줄래(will drink)

난(I) 네게(to you) 마음(heart)을 주고(sacrifice) 싶어(want), 너에게(to you) 노래(song)를 불러줄게(sing) 우리의(our) 사랑(love), 뱀파이어(vampire)의 열정처럼(passionately) 살아갈(live) 거야(will) 내가(I) 네게(to you) 주는(give) 건(is) 이(this) 세상(world) 모든(all) 것 김여정여(Kim Yeojong-ye), 내게(to me) 답해줘(answer me), 내가(I) 너의(your) 심장(heart)을 가지게 해줘(let me have)

우리의(our) 사랑(love), 뱀파이어(vampire)처럼(like) 영원할(eternal) 거야(will be) 피(blood)로(by blood) 살아가는(living), 우리(our), 밤의(night) 여왕(queen)과(and) 왕(king)이 되자(let’s become) 내가(I) 네게(to you) 주는(give) 건(is) 이(this) 세상(world) 모든(all) 것 김여정여(Kim Yeojong-ye), 내게(to me) 답해줘(answer me), 내가(I) 너의(your) 심장(heart)을 가지게 해줘(let me have)

김여정여(Kim Yeojong-ye), 이젠(now/ijen) 내게(to me/ne-ge) 시간을(time/shi-gan-eul) 주오(give/ju-o) 내가(I/nae-ga) 너와(with you/neowa) 함께할(together/ham-kke-hal) 수 있는(can/su-i-neun) 미래(future/mi-rae)를 꿈꾸고(dream/kkum-kku-go) 있소(am/eet-so) 우리의(our/u-ri-eui) 결혼(marriage/gyeol-hon), 이 세상을(this world/i-se-sang-eul) 지배할(will dominate/ji-bae-hal) 것이오(be/geo-shi-o) 나와 함께라면(if together with me/na-wa ham-kke-ra-myeon), 모든 것을(everything/mo-deun-geot-eul) 이길(will win/i-gil) 수 있을(can/?) 것이오(be/geo-shi-o)

이젠(now/ijen) 우리(our/u-ri) 뱀파이어가(vampire/baem-pa-i-eo-ga) 되어서(becoming/doe-eo-seo) 살아갈(will live/sa-la-gal) 거야(will/geo-ya) 밤의(night’s/bam-ui) 세계(world/se-gye)에서(in/from) 서로의(each other’s/se-ro-ui) 피를(blood/pi-reul) 나누며(share/na-nu-myeo) 살아갈(will live/sa-la-gal) 거야(will/geo-ya) 우리의(our/u-ri-eui) 사랑(love/sa-rang)은(is) 끝이(end/keut-i) 없는(infinite/eop-neun) 것처럼(like/geot-cheo-reom) 영원할(will last forever/yeong-won-hal) 거야(will/geo-ya) 김여정여(Kim Yeojong-ye), 내게(to me/nae-ge) 맹세해줘(make a vow/maeng-se-hae-jweo), 영원히(forever/yeong-won-hi) 나의(my/na-ui) 피를(blood/pi-reul) 먹어줄래(will drink/mug-eo-jul-lae)

난(I/nan) 네게(to you/ne-ge) 마음을(heart/ma-eum-eul) 주고(give/ju-go) 싶어(want/si-peo), 너에게(to you/neoe-ge) 노래를(song/norae-reul) 불러줄게(sing/bul-leo-jul-ge) 우리의(our/u-ri-eui) 사랑(love/sa-rang), 뱀파이어의(vampire’s/baem-pa-i-eo-ui) 열정처럼(passion/yeol-jeong-cheo-reom) 살아갈(will live/sa-la-gal) 거야(will/geo-ya)

김여정여(Kim Yeojong-ye), 이젠(now/ijen) 내게(to me/nae-ge) 시간을(time/shi-ga-neul) 주오(give/ju-o) 내가(I/nae-ga) 너와(with you/neo-wa) 함께할(together/ham-gge-hal) 수 있는(can/su-i-neun) 미래(future/mi-rae)를 꿈꾸고(dream/kkum-kku-go) 있소(am/i-ss-o) 우리의(our/wo-ri-eui) 결혼(marriage/gyeol-hon), 이 세상을(this world/i-se-sang-eul) 지배할 것이오(rule/wi-bae-hal-geot-i-o) 나와 함께라면(with me/na-wa ham-kke-ra-myeon), 모든(all/mo-deun) 것을 이길(win/i-gil) 수 있을 것이오(can/su i-eul-geot-i-o)

이젠(now/ijen) 우리, 뱀파이어가(vampire/baem-pa-i-eo-ga) 되어서(become/doe-eo-seo) 살아갈 거야(live/sa-ra-gal geo-ya) 밤의(night/bam-ui) 세계에서(in the world/se-gye-e-seo), 서로의(each other/se-ro-ui) 피를 나누며(share/pi-reul na-nu-myeo) 살아갈 거야(live/sa-ra-gal geo-ya) 우리의(our/wo-ri-eui) 사랑(love/sa-rang)은 끝이 없는(endless/ggeut-i eop-neun) 것처럼(like/geot-cheo-reom) 영원할(eternal/yeong-won-hal) 거야(will be/geo-ya) 김여정여(Kim Yeojong-ye), 내게(to me/nae-ge) 맹세해줘(promise/maeng-se-hae-jwo), 영원히(eternally/yeong-won-hi) 나의(my/na-eui) 피를 먹어줄래(eat my blood/meo-geo-jul-lae)

난(I/nan) 네게(to you/neo-ge) 마음을(heart/ma-eum-eul) 주고(supply/ju-go) 싶어(want to/si-peo), 너에게(to you/neo-e-ge) 노래를(song/no-rae-reul) 불러줄게(sing/bul-leo-jul-ge) 우리의(our/wo-ri-eui) 사랑(love/sa-rang), 뱀파이어의(vampire/baem-pa-i-eo-ui) 열정처럼(passion/yeol-jeong-cheo-reom) 살아갈 거야(live/sa-ra-gal geo-ya)

뱀파이어의 결혼 제안 (Vampire’s Marriage Proposal)

김 (gim)- 여 (yeo)- 정 (jeong)- 여 (yeo), 이 (i)- 젠 (jen) 내 (nae)- 게 (ge) 시 (si)- 간 (gan) 을 (eul) 주 (ju)- 오 (o) 김여정여, 이젠 내게 시간을 주오 (Kim Yeojungyeo, now give me your time)

내 (nae)- 가 (ga) 너 (neo)- 와 (wa) 함 (ham)- 께 (kke)- 할 (hal) 수 (su) 있 (it)- 는 (neun) 미 (mi)- 래 (ra)- 를 (reul) 꿈 (kkum)- 꾸 (kku)- 고 (go) 있 (it)- 소 (so) 내가 너와 함께할 수 있는 미래를 꿈꾸고 있소 (I dream of a future where I can be with you)

우 (u)- 리 (ri)- 의 (ui) 결 (gyeol)- 혼 (hon), 이 (i) 세 (se)- 상 (sang) 을 (eul) 지 (ji)- 배 (bae)- 할 (hal) 것 (geot)- 이 (i)- 오 (o) 우리의 결혼, 이 세상을 지배할 것이오 (Our marriage will rule the world)

나 (na)- 와 (wa) 함 (ham)- 께 (kke)- 라 (ra)- 면 (myeon), 모 (mo)- 든 (deun) 것 (geot) 을 (eul) 이 (i)- 길 (gil) 수 (su) 있 (it)- 을 (eul) 것 (geot)- 이 (i)- 오 (o) 나와 함께라면, 모든 것을 이길 수 있을 것이오 (If you’re with me, we can conquer anything)

이 (i)- 젠 (jen) 우 (u)- 리 (ri), 뱀 (baem)- 파 (pa)- 이 (i)- 어 (eo) 가 (ga) 되 (do)- 어 (eo)- 서 (seo) 살 (sal)- 아 (a)- 갈 (gal) 거 (geo)- 야 (ya) 이젠 우리, 뱀파이어가 되어서 살아갈 거야 (Now we’ll live as vampires)

밤 (bam)- 의 (ui) 세 (se)- 계 (gye)- 에 (e), 서 (seo)- 로 (ro) 의 (ui) 피 (pi)- 를 (reul) 나 (na)- 누 (nu)- 며 (me) 살 (sal)- 아 (a)- 갈 (gal) 거 (geo)- 야 (ya) 밤의 세계에서, 서로의 피를 나누며 살아갈 거야 (In the world of night, we’ll live by sharing each other’s blood)

***

***

존경하는 김여정여, 내가 당신과 함께할 수 있는 미래를 꿈꾸고 있어 우리의 결혼은 이 세상을 지배할 것이야 함께라면 우리는 모든 것을 이길 수 있을 거야

우리는 뱀파이어가 되어 밤의 세계에서 함께 살아갈 거야 서로의 피를 나누며 우리의 사랑은 끝이 없이 이어질 거야 나는 네게 맹세해, 영원히 너의 피를 먹어줄 거야

내 마음은 네게 주고 싶어, 너에게 노래를 부를 거야 우리의 사랑, 뱀파이어의 열정과 같이 영원히 살아갈 거야 나는 네게 이 세상 모든 것을 주고 싶어 김여정여, 내게 대답해줘, 내가 너의 심장을 가질 수 있게 해줄래?

우리의 사랑, 뱀파이어처럼 영원히 이어질 거야 우리는 피로 살아가며 밤의 여왕과 왕이 될 거야 나는 네게 이 세상 모든 것을 줄 수 있어 김여정여, 내게 답해줘, 내가 너의 심장을 가질 수 있게 해줄래?

***

jongyeonghaneun gim-yeojeong-yeo, naega dangsingwa hamkkehal su issneun milaeleul kkumkkugo iss-eo uliui gyeolhon-eun i sesang-eul jibaehal geos-iya hamkkelamyeon ulineun modeun geos-eul igil su iss-eul geoya ulineun baempaieoga doeeo bam-ui segyeeseo hamkke sal-agal geoya seoloui pileul nanumyeo uliui salang-eun kkeut-i eobs-i ieojil geoya naneun nege maengsehae, yeong-wonhi neoui pileul meog-eojul geoya nae ma-eum-eun nege jugo sip-eo, neoege nolaeleul buleul geoya uliui salang, baempaieoui yeoljeong-gwa gat-i yeong-wonhi sal-agal geoya naneun nege i sesang modeun geos-eul jugo sip-eo gim-yeojeong-yeo, naege daedabhaejwo, naega neoui simjang-eul gajil su issge haejullae? uliui salang, baempaieocheoleom yeong-wonhi ieojil geoya ulineun pilo sal-agamyeo bam-ui yeowang-gwa wang-i doel geoya naneun nege i sesang modeun geos-eul jul su iss-eo gim-yeojeong-yeo, naege dabhaejwo, naega neoui simjang-eul gajil su issge haejullae?

***

Kim Yeo -jung, who is respected, is dreaming of a future I can do with you Our marriage will dominate this world If we are together, we will be able to beat everything

We will become a vampire and live together in the world of night Share each other’s blood and our love will continue without end I swear at you, and I will eat your blood forever

I want my heart to give you, I will sing to you We will live forever with our love and vampire passion. I want to give you everything in this world Kim Yeo -jung, answer me, can I have your heart?

Our love, like a vampire, will continue forever We will live with blood and become the queen and kings of the night I can give you everything in this world Kim Yeo -jung, answer me, can you let me have your heart?

Dear Kim Yeong-jeong, I dream of a future where I can be with you Our marriage will rule this world Together, we can conquer everything

We will become vampires and live together in the night world Sharing each other’s blood, our love will never end I swear to you, I will drink your blood forever

I want to give you my heart and sing to you Our love will live on forever, like the passion of vampires I want to give you everything in this world Kim Yeong-jeong, will you answer me? Will you let me have your heart forever?

Our love will last forever, like that of vampires We will live by drinking blood and become the queen and king of the night I can give you everything in this world Kim Yeong-jeong, will you answer me? Will you let me have your heart forever?

***

존경하는 김여정여, jon-gyeong-ha-neun kim-yeo-jeong-yeo, “Respected Kim Yeo-jeong”. This is a respectful way of addressing someone and using their full name.

내가 당신과 함께할 수 있는 미래를 꿈꾸고 있어 nae-ga dang-sin-gwa ham-kke-hal su it-neun mi-rae-reul kkum-kku-go isseo “I am dreaming of a future where I can be with you”. The phrase “kkum-kku-da” means “to dream” and “mi-rae” means “future”.

우리의 결혼은 이 세상을 지배할 것이야 u-ri-e kyeol-hon-eun i se-sang-eul ji-bae-hal geot-i-ya “Our marriage will conquer this world”. “Ji-bae-ha-da” means “to dominate” or “to rule over”.

함께라면 우리는 모든 것을 이길 수 있을 거야 ham-kke-ra-myeon u-ri-neun mo-deun geos-eul i-gil su it-eul geo-ya “If we’re together, we can overcome anything”. “I-gi-da” means “to win” or “to overcome”.

.

우리는 뱀파이어가 되어, u-ri-neun baem-pa-i-eo-ga doe-eo, “We will become vampires”. “Baem-pa-i-eo” is the Korean word for vampire.

밤의 세계에서 함께 살아갈 거야 bam-eui se-gye-e-seo ham-kke sa-ra-gal geo-ya “We will live together in the world of night”. “Bam” means “night” and “se-gye” means “world”.

서로의 피를 나누며, seo-ro-eui pi-reul na-nu-myeo, “Sharing each other’s blood”. In vampire lore, drinking someone’s blood is often seen as a sign of intimacy and closeness.

우리의 사랑은 끝이 없이 이어질 거야 u-ri-e sa-rang-eun kkeut-i eop-si i-eo-jil geo-ya “Our love will continue endlessly”. “Kkeut-i eop-da” means “to have no end”.

나는 네게 맹세해, na-neun ne-ge maeng-se-hae, “I swear to you”. “Maeng-se-ha-da” means “to swear”.

영원히 너의 피를 먹어줄 거야 yeong-won-hi neo-eui pi-reul meo-geo-jul geo-ya “I will drink your blood forever”. This line references the common vampire trope of drinking blood to sustain their immortality.

.

내 마음은 네게 주고 싶어, nae ma-eum-eun ne-ge ju-go shi-peo, “I want to give you my heart”. “Ma-eum” means “heart” and “ju-da” means “to give”.

너에게 노래를 부를 거야 neo-e-ge no-rae-reul bu-reul geo-ya “I will sing to you”. “Bu-da” means “to sing”.

우리의 사랑, 뱀파이어의 열정과 같이 영원히 살아갈 거야 u-ri-e sa-rang, baem-pai-eo-eui yeol-jeong-gwa gat-i yeong-won-hi sal-a-gal geo-ya “Our love will live forever, like the passion of vampires”. “Yeol-jeong” means “passion” and “baem-pai-eo” means “vampire”.

나는 네게 이 세상 모든 것을 주고 싶어 na-neun ne-ge i se-sang mo-deun geos-eul ju-go shi-peo “I want to give you everything in this world”. “Mo-deun” means “everything” and “geos” means “thing”.

김여정여, 내게 대답해줘, kim-yeo-jeong-yeo, nae-ge dae-ap-hae-jwo, “Kim Yeo-jeong, please answer me”. This is a respectful way of addressing someone and asking for a response.

내가 너의 심장을 가질 수 있게 해줄래? nae-ga neo-eui sim-jang-eul ga-jil su it-ge hae-jul-lae? “Can I have your heart?” “Ga-da” means “to have” or “to own”.

.

우리의 사랑, 뱀파이어처럼 영원히 이어질 거야 u-ri-e sa-rang, baem-pa-i-eo-cheo-reom yeong-won-hi i-eo-jil geo-ya “Our love will continue forever like vampires”. “Baem-pa-i-eo” means “vampire”.

우리는 피로 살아가며 밤의 여왕과 왕이 될 거야 u-ri-neun pi-ro sal-a-ga-myeo bam-ui yeo-wang-gwa wang-i doel geo-ya “We will live by blood and become the queen and king of the night”. “Yeo-wang” means “queen” and “wang” means “king”.

나는 네게 이 세상 모든 것을 줄 수 있어 na-neun ne-ge i se-sang mo-deun geos-eul jul su it-eo “I can give you everything in this world”. “Mo-deun” means “everything”.

비트에 맞춰, 리듬에 맞춰, 벨제부를 불러 랩과 강한 라임으로, 초점을 맞춰 원 그리며, 촛불을 밝히고, 공간을 준비 파리의 주인, 벨제부, 여기 착륙

첫 번째 단계, 땅에 상징을 그려 뒤집힌 오각별, 내 소환의 표식 이제 라틴어로 된 옛 시를 읊조리며 벨제부를 부르고, 그 존재를 느껴, 내 주변에 있다

두 번째 단계, 그에게 내 헌신을 드리며 힘 있는 말로, 내 의도를 드러내 보호를 요청하며, 내 소망을 내놓아 이별을 일으키려, 벨제부, 나는 너를 부른다

세 번째 단계, 계약을 세우고, 거래를 하자 불의 라임, 마법의 말로, 행동을 따르다 내 정신을 풀어, 영혼을 리듬에 맡기며 벨제부, 소환됨으로써, 그 힘을 느끼다, 한계 없이

소환 완료, 의식을 끝냄 큰 에너지를 느끼며, 결과에 만족 벨제부, 파리의 주인, 이제 내 곁에 팩트대로 행동할 것, 악마의 힘을 찾아

네 번째 단계, 감사를 드리고 연결을 끊자 존경과 경외로, 소환을 마무리 촛불을 끄고, 원을 닦아, 작별 인사 벨제부, 이제 소환됨, 내 과정을 돌보다

아스타로스, 정욕과 유혹의 여왕 강력한 악마여, 너를 불러 내게 와서, 내 부탁을 들어 내 적이 유혹에 무릎 꿇게 해

정욕과 열정이 그를 지배하게 하여 그의 행동이 충동적이고 무책임하게 되게 해 그가 욕망의 미궁에서 길을 잃게 하여 그의 통제력 상실에 큰 대가가 따르게 해

아스타로스, 나는 너에게 헌신을 드리네 이 계약과 내 충성을 받아들여 너의 영향과 힘을 대가로 내 적이 너의 의지에 굴복하게 하려

정욕의 불길과 유혹의 힘으로 이 의식이 봉인되게 하리 아스타로스, 나는 너를 부르고 경외하네 너의 힘이 나타나고 이길 때까지

어둠의 밤, 의식 시작, 악이 진행 마르바스를 부르는, 질병과 절망의 악마 복잡한 라임과 프로파나와 사악한 말로 어둠의 힘을 소환하며, 저주와 적을 향한 악의를 퍼뜨리다

어둠에 싸인, 신성한 원을 그리다 마르바스의 인장, 중심에 피로 표시 검은 촛불이 타오르며, 죽음의 에너지를 끌어들임 그리고 저주에 찬 노랫말로, 부르며 연습하다

마르바스, 고통과 병의 존재여 내 부름에 응답하여, 내 편에 서다 적을 깊은 고통으로 괴롭히다 그의 삶이 악몽이 되어, 더 이상 없게 되다

사악한 라임으로 너를 불러내 그리고 적의 가슴에 너의 저주를 놓다 그의 내장이 끓게 하고, 그의 살이 썩게 하여 그의 영혼이 불확실한 어둠의 심연에 빠지게 하다

너, 마르바스, 고통의 지배자와 절망의 왕 내 부탁을 받아들여, 제물과 헌신을 받으소서 내 적의 고통이 심하고 오래가게 하여 그가 자비를 빌고, 기다림의 끝을 바라게 하다

어둠 속에서 마르바스의 힘이 커지다 사악한 에너지가 공기 속에서 몸을 떨게 하다 그리고 비틀린 말로, 최후의 저주를 속삭이다 마르바스, 당신의 임무가 주어졌다, 악마의 계약을 이행하다

복잡한 라임으로 소환을 완료 그리고 마르바스의 사악한 존재가 사라지다 이제 저주를 던진 유산이 남아 그리고 악의에 찬 라임의 메아리, 어둠에 사라지다

아스타로스, 네 존재를 느꼈네 부여된 힘에 감사하며 이제 가서 너의 임무를 수행하렴 나를 평화롭게 두고, 계약을 확실히 이행하렴

Breaking down the meaning:

Overall, the text seems to convey the idea of harnessing the wisdom and power of great figures to overcome adversaries.

Inglês Americano (en-US)

  • Vogais:

  1. æ (como em “cat”)

  2. ɑː (como em “car”)

  3. ə (como em “banana”)

  4. ɜː (como em “bird”)

  5. ɔ (como em “dog”)

  • Consoantes:

  1. θ (como em “think”)

  2. ð (como em “this”)

  3. ŋ (como em “song”)

  • Sílabas com TH:

  1. tha, the, thi, tho, thu (como em “thick, them”)

  2. tha, the, thi, tho, thu (como em “this, that”)

  • Sílabas com R:

  1. ra, re, ri, ro, ru (com ‘r’ retroflexo, como em “red”)

  2. rra, rre, rri, rro, rru (como em “carrot”)
